**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0`

- Use `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-k8s-arch-001: Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture

## Task

Explain the Kubernetes scheduler architecture and how a Pod gets assigned to a Node. Trace the complete scheduling pipeline from when a Pod enters the scheduling queue to when it is bound to a Node, including the plugin framework, extension points, and the two-phase (scheduling cycle + binding cycle) design.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~2.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: pkg/scheduler/ — the kube-scheduler component

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the scheduler subsystem (scheduler core, framework, queue, cache, plugins)
2. Trace the dependency chain from the main scheduling loop through the scheduling cycle and binding cycle
3. Document the plugin framework architecture (extension points: PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit, Bind)
4. Explain how the SchedulingQueue, Cache, and CycleState interact during a scheduling cycle

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes scheduler architecture and written it to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

## Key Findings

I traced the complete scheduling pipeline from pod enqueue to binding:

**Files Analyzed (8 core components):**
- `scheduler.go` - Main orchestration and Run loop
- `schedule_one.go` - Entry point + two-phase scheduling pipeline  
- `framework/interface.go` - Plugin interface definitions
- `framework/runtime/framework.go` - Plugin orchestration
- `internal/cache/interface.go` - Pod/node state management
- `internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go` - Pod queue management

**Two-Phase Design:**
1. **Scheduling Cycle** (sync): PreFilter → Filter → Score → Reserve → Permit
2. **Binding Cycle** (async): WaitOnPermit → PreBind → Bind → PostBind

**Key Architectural Insights:**
- **Optimistic concurrency**: Pod assumed in cache immediately, recovers gracefully on binding failure
- **Snapshot consistency**: Frozen cache state during scoring phase prevents inconsistencies
- **Plugin framework**: 13 extension points with clear separation (filtering/scoring/reservation/binding)
- **Parallel operations**: Filter and Score phases parallelized across nodes
- **Status machine**: Each plugin phase has defined success/failure paths with cleanup

The analysis document includes the complete 20-step dependency chain, component interactions, error handling strategies, and architectural patterns that enable both high throughput and correctness in pod scheduling.

Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders \\t\\tresult, status := fwk.RunPostFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod, fitError.Diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\\n177: \\t\\tmsg := status.Message()\\n178: \\t\\tfitError.Diagnosis.PostFilterMsg = msg\\n179: Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. These plugins are called\\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\\n444: \\tPlugin\\n445: \\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\\n446: \\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n447: \\t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\\n448: \\t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\\n449: \\t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n450: \\t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n451: \\t//\\n452: \\t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\\n453: \\t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n454: \\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n455: \\t//\\n456: \\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\\n457: \\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\\n458: \\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\\n459: \\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\\n460: \\t//\\n461: \\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\\n462: \\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. These plugins should\\n506: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\\n507: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\\n508: // rejection of the pod.\\n509: type ReservePlugin interface {\\n510: \\tPlugin\\n511: \\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\\n512: \\t// updated. Permit\\n548: \\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\\n549: \\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\\n550: \\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\\n551: \\t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \\\"wait\\\", the framework will wait only\\n552: \\t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\\n553: \\tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\\n554: }\\n555: \\n556: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Bind\\\" plugins. Plugins\n662: // must store and use this handle to call framework functions.\n663: type Handle interface {\n664: \t// PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\n665: \tPodNominator\n666: \t// PluginsRunner abstracts operations to run some plugins.\n667: \tPluginsRunner\n668: \t// SnapshotSharedLister returns listers from the latest NodeInfo Snapshot. The snapshot\n669: \t// is taken at the beginning of a scheduling cycle and remains unchanged until\n670: \t// a pod finishes \"Permit\" point.\n671: \t//\n672: \t// It should be used only during scheduling cycle:\n673: \t// - There is no guarantee that the information remains unchanged in the binding phase of scheduling.\n674: \t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in the binding cycle s.Reasons()...)\n924: \t\t// Record the first failed plugin unless we proved that\n925: \t\t// the latter is more relevant.\n926: \t\tif len(rejectorPlugin) == 0 {\n927: \t\t\trejectorPlugin = runPostFilterPlugin(ctx context.Context, pl framework.PostFilterPlugin, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap framework.NodeToStatusMap) (*framework.PostFilterResult, \treturn r, s\n942: }\n943: \n944: // RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods runs the set of configured filter plugins\n945: // for nominated pod on the given node.\n946: // This function is called from two different places: Schedule and Preempt.\n947: // When it is called from Schedule, we want to test whether the pod is\n948: // schedulable on the node with all the existing pods on the node plus higher\n949: // and equal priority pods nominated to run on the node.\n950: // When it is called from Preempt, we should remove the victims of preemption\n951: // and add the nominated pods. Removal of the victims is done by\n952: // SelectVictimsOnNode(). Preempt removes victims from PreFilter state and\n953: // NodeInfo before calling this function.\n954: func (f *frameworkImpl) RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx context.Context, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, info *framework.NodeInfo) *framework.Status {\n955: \tvar status *framework.Status\n956: \n957: \tpodsAdded := false\n958: \t// We run filters twice in some cases. If the node has greater or equal priority\n959: \t// nominated pods, we run them when those pods are added to PreFilter state and nodeInfo.\n960: \t// If all filters succeed in this pass, we run them again when these\n961: \t// nominated pods are not added. This second pass is necessary because some\n962: \t// filters such as inter-pod affinity may not pass without the nominated pods.\n963: \t// If there are no nominated pods for the node or if the first run of the\n964: \t// filters fail, we don't run the second pass.\n965: \t// We consider only equal or higher priority pods in the first pass, because\n966: \t// those are the current \"pod\" must yield to them and not take a space opened\n967: \t// for running them. It is ok if the current \"pod\" take resources freed for\n968: \t// lower priority pods.\n969: \t// Requiring that the new pod is schedulable in both circumstances ensures that\n970: \t// we are making a conservative decision: filters like resources and inter-pod\n971: \t// anti-affinity are more likely to fail when the nominated pods are treated\n972: \t// as running, while filters like pod affinity are more likely to fail when\n973: \t// the nominated pods are treated as not running. We can't just assume the\n974: \t// nominated pods are running because they are not running right now and in fact,\n975: \t// they may end up getting scheduled to a different node.\n976: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n977: \tlogger = klog.LoggerWithName(logger, \"FilterWithNominatedPods\")\n978: \tctx = klog.NewContext(ctx, logger)\n979: \tfor i := 0; i < 2; i++ {\n980: \t\tstateToUse := state\n981: \t\tnodeInfoToUse := info\n982: \t\tif i == 0 {\n983: \t\t\tvar err error\n984: \t\t\tpodsAdded, stateToUse, nodeInfoToUse, err = addNominatedPods(ctx, f, pod, state, info)\n985: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n986: \t\t\t\treturn framework.AsStatus(err)\n987: \t\t\t}\n988: \t\t} else if !podsAdded || !status.IsSuccess() {\n989: \t\t\tbreak\n990: \t\t}\n991: \n992: \t\tstatus = f.RunFilterPlugins(ctx, stateToUse, pod, nodeInfoToUse)\n993: \t\tif !status.IsSuccess() && !status.IsRejected() {\n994: \t\t\treturn status\n995: \t\t}\n996: \t}\n997: \n998: \treturn status\n999: }\n1000: \n1001: // addNominatedPods adds pods with equal or greater priority which are nominated\n1002: // to run on the node. We don't have guaranteed delivery of all events:\\n30: // We use Reflector to list and watch from remote.\\n31: // Reflector might be slow and do a relist, which would lead to missing events.\\n32: //\\n33: // State Machine of a pod's events in scheduler's cache:\\n34: //\\n35: //\\t+-------------------------------------------+  +----+\\n36: //\\t|                            Add            |  |    |\\n37: //\\t|                                           |  |    | Update\\n38: //\\t+      Assume                Add            v  v    |\\n39: //\\n40: // Initial +--------> Assumed +------------+---> Added <--+\\n41: //\\n42: //\\t^                +   +               |       +\\n43: //\\t|                |   |               |       |\\n44: //\\t|                |   |           Add |       | Remove\\n45: //\\t|                |   |               |       |\\n46: //\\t|                |   |               +       |\\n47: //\\t+----------------+   +-----------> Expired   +----> Deleted\\n48: //\\t      Forget             Expire\\n49: //\\n50: // Note that an assumed pod can expire, because if we haven't received Add event notifying us\\n51: // for a while, there might be some problems and we shouldn't keep the pod in cache anymore.\\n52: //\\n53: // Note that \\\"Initial\\\", \\\"Expired\\\", and \\\"Deleted\\\" pods do not actually exist in cache.\\n54: // Based on existing use cases, we are making the following assumptions:\\n55: //   - No pod would be assumed twice\\n56: //   - A pod could be added without going through scheduler. In this case, we will see Add but not Assume event.\\n57: //   - If a pod wasn't added, it wouldn't be removed or updated.\\n58: //   - Both \\\"Expired\\\" and \\\"Deleted\\\" are valid end states. In case of some problems, e.g. network issue,\\n59: //     a pod might have changed its state (e.g. added and deleted) without delivering notification to the cache.\\n60: type Cache interface {\\n61: \\t// NodeCount returns the number of nodes in the cache.\\n62: \\t// DO NOT use outside of tests.\\n63: \\tNodeCount() int\\n64: \\n65: \\t// PodCount returns the number of pods in the cache (including those from deleted nodes).\\n66: \\t// DO NOT use outside of tests.\\n67: \\tPodCount() (int, error)\\n68: \\n69: \\t// AssumePod assumes a pod scheduled and aggregates the pod's information into its node.\\n70: \\t// The implementation also decides the policy to expire pod before being confirmed (receiving Add event).\\n71: \\t// After expiration, its information would be subtracted.\\n72: \\tAssumePod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n73: \\n74: \\t// FinishBinding signals that cache for assumed pod can be expired\\n75: \\tFinishBinding(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n76: \\n77: \\t// ForgetPod removes an assumed pod from cache.\\n78: \\tForgetPod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n79: \\n80: \\t// AddPod either confirms a pod if it's assumed, or adds it back if it's expired.\\n81: \\t// If added back, the pod's information would be added again.\\n82: \\tAddPod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n83: \\n84: \\t// UpdatePod removes oldPod's information and adds newPod's information.\\n85: \\tUpdatePod(logger klog.Logger, oldPod, newPod *v1.Pod) error\\n86: \\n87: \\t// RemovePod removes a pod. We don't have guaranteed delivery of all events:\n30: // We use Reflector to list and watch from remote.\n31: // Reflector might be slow and do a relist, which would lead to missing events.\n32: //\n33: // State Machine of a pod's events in scheduler's cache:\n34: //\n35: //\t+-------------------------------------------+  +----+\n36: //\t|                            Add            |  |    |\n37: //\t|                                           |  |    | Update\n38: //\t+      Assume                Add            v  v    |\n39: //\n40: // Initial +--------> Assumed +------------+---> Added <--+\n41: //\n42: //\t^                +   +               |       +\n43: //\t|                |   |               |       |\n44: //\t|                |   |           Add |       | Remove\n45: //\t|                |   |               |       |\n46: //\t|                |   |               +       |\n47: //\t+----------------+   +-----------> Expired   +----> Deleted\n48: //\t      Forget             Expire\n49: //\n50: // Note that an assumed pod can expire, because if we haven't received Add event notifying us\n51: // for a while, there might be some problems and we shouldn't keep the pod in cache anymore.\n52: //\n53: // Note that \"Initial\", \"Expired\", and \"Deleted\" pods do not actually exist in cache.\n54: // Based on existing use cases, we are making the following assumptions:\n55: //   - No pod would be assumed twice\n56: //   - A pod could be added without going through scheduler. In this case, we will see Add but not Assume event.\n57: //   - If a pod wasn't added, it wouldn't be removed or updated.\n58: //   - Both \"Expired\" and \"Deleted\" are valid end states. In case of some problems, e.g. network issue,\n59: //     a pod might have changed its state (e.g. added and deleted) without delivering notification to the cache.\n60: type Cache interface {\n61: \t// NodeCount returns the number of nodes in the cache.\n62: \t// DO NOT use outside of tests.\n63: \tNodeCount() int\n64: \n65: \t// PodCount returns the number of pods in the cache (including those from deleted nodes).\n66: \t// DO NOT use outside of tests.\n67: \tPodCount() (int, error)\n68: \n69: \t// AssumePod assumes a pod scheduled and aggregates the pod's information into its node.\n70: \t// The implementation also decides the policy to expire pod before being confirmed (receiving Add event).\n71: \t// After expiration, its information would be subtracted.\n72: \tAssumePod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n73: \n74: \t// FinishBinding signals that cache for assumed pod can be expired\n75: \tFinishBinding(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n76: \n77: \t// ForgetPod removes an assumed pod from cache.\n78: \tForgetPod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n79: \n80: \t// AddPod either confirms a pod if it's assumed, or adds it back if it's expired.\n81: \t// If added back, the pod's information would be added again.\n82: \tAddPod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n83: \n84: \t// UpdatePod removes oldPod's information and adds newPod's information.\n85: \tUpdatePod(logger klog.Logger, oldPod, newPod *v1.Pod) error\n86: \n87: \t// RemovePod removes a pod. The pod's information would be subtracted from assigned node.\n88: \tRemovePod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n89: \n90: \t// GetPod returns the pod from the cache with the same namespace and the\n91: \t// same name of the specified pod.\n92: \tGetPod(pod *v1.Pod) (*v1.Pod, error)\n93: \n94: \t// IsAssumedPod returns true if the pod is assumed and not expired.\n95: \tIsAssumedPod(pod *v1.Pod) (bool, error)\n96: \n97: \t// AddNode adds overall information about node.\n98: \t// It returns a clone of added NodeInfo object.\n99: \tAddNode(logger klog.Logger, node *v1.Node) *framework.NodeInfo\n100: \n101: \t// UpdateNode updates overall information about node.\n102: \t// It returns a clone of updated NodeInfo object.\n103: \tUpdateNode(logger klog.Logger, oldNode, newNode *v1.Node) *framework.NodeInfo\n104: \n105: \t// RemoveNode removes overall information about node.\n106: \tRemoveNode(logger klog.Logger, node *v1.Node) error\n107: \n108: \t// UpdateSnapshot updates the passed infoSnapshot to the current contents of Cache.\n109: \t// The node info contains aggregated information of pods scheduled (including assumed to be)\n110: \t// on this node.\n111: \t// The snapshot only includes Nodes that are not deleted at the time this function is called.\n112: \t// nodeinfo.Node() is guaranteed to be not nil for all the nodes in the snapshot.\n113: \tUpdateSnapshot(logger klog.Logger, nodeSnapshot *Snapshot) error\n114: \n115: \t// Dump produces a dump of the current cache.\n116: \tDump() *Dump\n117: }\n118: \n119: // Dump is a dump of the cache state.\n120: type Dump struct {\n121: \tAssumedPods sets.Set[string]\n122: \tNodes       map[string]*framework.NodeInfo\n123: }\n124: ",

  "content": "# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** \u2014 Main Scheduler struct that orchestrates the scheduling loop, initializes frameworks, queues, and cache; implements the Run() method that starts the scheduling process\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** \u2014 Contains ScheduleOne() entry point and the two-phase scheduling pipeline (schedulingCycle and bindingCycle); implements findNodesThatFitPod, prioritizeNodes, selectHost\n\n### Framework Architecture\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** \u2014 Defines all plugin interfaces (PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), Framework interface, CycleState, Status codes, and extension points\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** \u2014 frameworkImpl implementation that instantiates and orchestrates plugins; implements all Run* methods (RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins, etc.)\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** \u2014 CycleState passes mutable data between plugins within a scheduling cycle\n\n### Internal Components\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** \u2014 Cache interface defining pod/node state management with Assume/Forget/Add/Remove operations and snapshot semantics\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** \u2014 Cache implementation tracking assumed pods and node information with expiration policy\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** \u2014 Snapshot provides read-only view of cache state at beginning of scheduling cycle\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** \u2014 SchedulingQueue manages pods to be scheduled with activeQ, backoffQ, and unschedulableQ; handles pod lifecycle\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### Entry Point: Main Scheduling Loop\n1. **Scheduler.Run(ctx)** (scheduler.go:435)\n   - Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Run()` to start queue processor\n   - Spawns goroutine calling `sched.ScheduleOne()` in a loop\n\n### Phase 1: Per-Pod Scheduling (ScheduleOne)\n2. **Scheduler.ScheduleOne(ctx)** (schedule_one.go:66)\n   - Pops next pod from queue via `sched.NextPod()`\n   - Calls `sched.SchedulePod()` which routes to `sched.schedulePod()`\n   - If **schedulingCycle** succeeds, spawns async goroutine for **bindingCycle**\n\n3. **Scheduler.schedulePod()** (schedule_one.go:390)\n   - **Scheduling Cycle** orchestration:\n     - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod()` to filter nodes\n     - Calls `prioritizeNodes()` to score and rank nodes\n     - Returns ScheduleResult with suggested node\n\n### Scheduling Cycle: Finding Best Node\n4. **Scheduler.findNodesThatFitPod()** (schedule_one.go:442)\n   - Updates cache snapshot: `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n   - **Runs PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()`\n     - Returns PreFilterResult (may reduce candidate nodes to a subset)\n   - **Runs Filter plugins** via `findNodesThatPassFilters()` (in parallel)\n     - Filters nodes based on framework and extender filters\n   - Returns list of feasible nodes\n\n5. **Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:679)\n   - Iterates through preFilterPlugins in order\n   - Each plugin can:\n     - Return Success with optional PreFilterResult (NodeNames subset)\n     - Return Skip (coupled Filter plugins are skipped)\n     - Return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable (stops immediately on latter)\n   - Merges PreFilterResults via intersection if multiple plugins filter nodes\n\n6. **Scheduler.findNodesThatPassFilters()** (schedule_one.go:573)\n   - **Runs Filter plugins** in parallel via parallelize framework\n   - For each node: `fwk.RunFilterPlugins()` (all filter plugins run sequentially per node)\n   - Stops early if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached (based on percentageOfNodesToScore)\n\n7. **Framework.RunFilterPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:842)\n   - Iterates through filterPlugins sequentially\n   - Each plugin returns Success or Unschedulable for a given node\n   - First failed plugin rejects the node; framework records plugin status\n\n### Scoring Phase: Ranking Feasible Nodes\n8. **prioritizeNodes()** (schedule_one.go:745)\n   - **Runs PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n   - **Runs Score plugins** via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n   - **Runs extenders** (parallel) if configured\n   - Combines all scores into NodePluginScores with TotalScore\n\n9. **Framework.RunScorePlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1089+)\n   - For each score plugin:\n     - Calls Score() for each feasible node (parallel across nodes)\n     - Calls NormalizeScore() to normalize all scores for that plugin (0-100)\n   - Aggregates scores from all plugins weighted by plugin weights\n\n10. **selectHost()** (schedule_one.go:863)\n    - Uses reservoir sampling from highest-scored nodes\n    - Returns top node and optionally top-N nodes for reporting\n\n### Assumption Phase: Optimistic Concurrency\n11. **Scheduler.schedulingCycle()** (schedule_one.go:138)\n    - After SchedulePod succeeds, calls `sched.assume()` to mark pod on chosen node\n    - **Runs Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()`\n    - **Runs Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()`\n    - If any plugin fails:\n      - Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` to cleanup\n      - Calls `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()` to undo assumption\n    - Returns on success or moves pod to next phase\n\n12. **Scheduler.assume()** (schedule_one.go:870+)\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.AssumePod()` to assume pod on node\n    - Cache updates nodeInfo with pod's resources\n\n13. **Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve()** (runtime/framework.go:1149)\n    - Iterates through reservePlugins\n    - Each plugin can reserve resources or perform setup for the pod\n    - Failure stops immediately and triggers Unreserve on all prior plugins\n\n14. **Framework.RunPermitPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1169)\n    - Each plugin returns Status and optional timeout\n    - Success: proceed immediately\n    - Wait: pod enters waiting pod map (framework tracks waiting state)\n    - Reject/Error: trigger cleanup (Unreserve + ForgetPod)\n\n### Phase 2: Binding Cycle (Async)\n15. **Scheduler.bindingCycle()** (schedule_one.go:264)\n    - **WaitOnPermit()**: If pod was permitted to wait, blocks here\n    - **RunPreBindPlugins()**: Pre-binding setup plugins\n    - **bind()**: Calls Bind plugins to actually bind pod\n    - **RunPostBindPlugins()**: Post-binding cleanup plugins\n\n16. **Framework.WaitOnPermit()** (runtime/framework.go:1186)\n    - Waits on permit.WaitingPods map for pod's UID\n    - Returns Success (approved) or Rejected (denied)\n\n17. **Scheduler.bind()** (schedule_one.go:958)\n    - **RunBindPlugins()**: Calls Bind plugins\n    - First plugin to return non-Skip binds pod (sets NodeName)\n    - Default Bind plugin writes binding to API server\n\n18. **Framework.RunPostBindPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1304)\n    - Informational only; no failure handling\n    - Plugins can perform cleanup after binding succeeds\n\n### Failure Handling\n19. **Scheduler.handleSchedulingFailure()** (schedule_one.go:1012)\n    - Called when schedulingCycle fails\n    - If PostFilterPlugins exist, runs preemption to evict lower-priority pods\n    - Calls failure handler which may requeue pod with backoff\n\n20. **Scheduler.handleBindingCycleError()** (schedule_one.go:324)\n    - Called when bindingCycle fails\n    - Cleans up: RunReservePluginsUnreserve() + ForgetPod()\n    - Moves related pods from unschedulable queue back to active/backoff queue\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Pattern: Two-Phase Scheduling with Optimistic Concurrency\n\n**Problem Solved:**\n- Binding is slow (API server write) and can fail\n- Blocking scheduling on binding would be inefficient\n- Need to continue scheduling other pods while binding completes\n\n**Solution:**\n1. **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Find node and assume pod on it in cache\n2. **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Actually bind pod to cluster, with failure recovery\n\n**Key Insight:** Cache assumption creates optimistic lock\n- Pod is considered scheduled in cache immediately\n- Other pods can't use same resources (Assume adds pod to nodeInfo)\n- If binding fails, Forget removes pod and resources are returned to unschedulable queue\n- Other pods scheduled during binding period already see reserved resources\n\n### Plugin Framework: Extension Points\n\nThe framework defines **13 extension points** where plugins can hook in:\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous):**\n- **PreFilter**: Early filtering (can skip Filter plugins entirely)\n- **Filter**: Feasibility check per node\n- **PostFilter**: Preemption/remediation if pod unschedulable\n- **PreScore**: Preparation before scoring (informational)\n- **Score**: Rank nodes 0-100 (parallel per plugin, serial per node)\n- **Reserve**: Resource booking after node chosen\n\n**Permit/Waiting:**\n- **Permit**: Gate before binding (can wait for external events)\n\n**Binding Cycle (Async):**\n- **PreBind**: Pre-binding setup (can still reject)\n- **Bind**: Actually bind pod (default writes to API server)\n- **PostBind**: Cleanup after successful binding (no failures)\n\n**Queue Management:**\n- **PreEnqueue**: Pre-enqueue filtering\n- **QueueSort**: Pod priority ordering\n- **EnqueueExtensions**: Event-driven requeuing hints\n\n### Component Interactions\n\n**1. SchedulingQueue \u2194 Scheduler**\n- Queue holds unscheduled pods in activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulableQ\n- Scheduler.NextPod() pops highest-priority pod\n- Queue.Done(uid) marks pod done after binding\n- Queue.Activate() moves pods between queues on cluster events\n\n**2. Cache \u2194 Framework**\n- Cache maintains assumed pod state and node information\n- UpdateSnapshot() captures cache state at scheduling cycle start\n- Framework.SnapshotSharedLister() provides read-only view to plugins\n- AssumePod() is called after Reserve plugins pass\n- ForgetPod() reverts assumption on failure\n\n**3. CycleState \u2194 Plugins**\n- CycleState is thread-safe mutable map passed to each plugin\n- PreFilter plugins write initial computed state\n- Filter/Score plugins read and optionally update state\n- Reserve/Permit plugins register cleanup actions\n- PreFilterExtensions use state for incremental updates during preemption\n\n**4. Framework \u2194 Extenders**\n- Legacy extensibility mechanism (pre-plugin era)\n- Extenders participate in Filter and Prioritize phases\n- Extenders run after framework plugins\n- Integration: DefaultPreemption plugin can coordinate with extenders\n\n### Data Flow: Pod Perspective\n\n```\nPod \u2192 SchedulingQueue (activeQ)\n   \u2193\nPod.Pop() \u2192 ScheduleOne()\n   \u2193\nScheduling Cycle:\n   - PreFilter plugins: Extract pod requirements, filter nodes\n   - Filter plugins: Test pod feasibility on remaining nodes (parallel)\n   - PreScore plugins: Setup scoring state (informational)\n   - Score plugins: Rank feasible nodes (parallel per plugin)\n   \u2193\n   Find best node via selectHost() \u2192 Assume pod on node in cache\n   \u2193\n   Reserve plugins: Book resources\n   Permit plugins: Gate binding\n   \u2193 (if all pass)\n   Binding Cycle (async goroutine):\n   - WaitOnPermit(): Wait for permit plugin approval\n   - PreBind plugins: Final checks\n   - Bind plugins: Write binding to API server\n   - PostBind plugins: Cleanup\n   \u2193\nPod is scheduled (NodeName set, binding recorded)\n```\n\n### Parallelization Strategy\n\n**Parallel Operations:**\n- **Filter plugins**: Parallelized across nodes (via parallelize.Parallelizer)\n  - Each node tests all filter plugins sequentially\n  - Early termination stops other nodes if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached\n- **Score plugins**: Parallelized across nodes\n  - Each score plugin evaluates all nodes in parallel\n  - NormalizeScore is sequential per plugin\n- **Extenders**: Parallelized across extenders (via goroutines)\n  - Each extender runs independently with mutex for aggregating scores\n\n**Sequential Operations:**\n- Filter plugins per node (can't parallelize within single node)\n- PreFilter and PostFilter plugins (must run sequentially, early termination possible)\n- Reserve, Permit, PreBind plugins (state dependencies)\n\n### Error Handling Strategy\n\n**Success Paths:**\n- All PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit plugins return Success \u2192 pod assigned\n\n**Failure Paths:**\n\n1. **PreFilter or Filter Failure:**\n   - Triggers PostFilter plugins (preemption)\n   - PostFilter plugins can attempt to make pod schedulable\n   - If PostFilter returns Success + NominatingInfo, pod saved for retry\n   - If PostFilter returns Unschedulable, pod goes to unschedulableQ + backoff\n\n2. **Reserve Failure:**\n   - Immediately triggers Unreserve on all prior Reserve plugins\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod requeued to backoffQ\n\n3. **Permit Failure:**\n   - Same cleanup as Reserve failure\n   - If rejected, pod marked and won't be re-tried immediately\n\n4. **Binding Cycle Failure:**\n   - Reserve plugins Unreserved\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod moved to unschedulableQ or backoffQ based on failure reason\n   - Cluster events may trigger requeuing\n\n### Status Codes and Their Meanings\n\n- **Success**: Plugin succeeded, pod can continue or is OK\n- **Error**: Unexpected internal error; pod requeued to activeQ/backoffQ\n- **Unschedulable**: Pod can't fit but may fit after cluster changes (e.g., node capacity increases); pod backed off\n- **UnschedulableAndUnresolvable**: Pod fundamentally unschedulable; pod backed off but PostFilter won't help\n- **Wait** (Permit only): Pod waiting for external event; entered waiting pod map\n- **Skip**: PreFilter/PreScore can skip coupled Filter/Score plugins; BindPlugin can skip binding\n- **Pending** (Reserve/PreBind only): Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external component (e.g., DRA device driver)\n\n### Snapshot Design: Read-Consistency Guarantee\n\n**Why Snapshots?**\n- Plugins run over many milliseconds; cluster state changes during scheduling\n- Without snapshot, plugins could see inconsistent state\n- Snapshot provides frozen view at cycle start\n\n**When Taken:**\n- At start of schedulePod(): `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(nodeInfoSnapshot)`\n- Snapshot remains unchanged through PreFilter \u2192 Filter \u2192 PreScore \u2192 Score\n\n**Snapshot Guarantees:**\n- All Filter decisions based on same node state\n- Score plugins see same node state\n- If pod preempted nodes before score phase, preemption not reflected in snapshot\n\n**Binding Phase:**\n- Can't use snapshot (cluster state has changed during scoring)\n- Plugins use live informers instead\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase architecture combining **synchronous scheduling (find + assume) with asynchronous binding**. This decouples slow API operations from scheduling throughput.\n\nThe **plugin framework** provides 13 extension points with clear separation of concerns: filtering (feasibility), scoring (preference), reservation (resource booking), and binding (commitment). Plugins are orchestrated via a state machine with careful failure handling and recovery mechanisms.\n\n**Key architectural decisions:**\n1. **Optimistic concurrency**: Assume in cache, recover on binding failure\n2. **Snapshot consistency**: Frozen cache view for scheduling decisions\n3. **Progressive filtering**: Early termination when enough feasible nodes found\n4. **Parallel scoring**: Independent plugin evaluation across nodes\n5. **Permit gating**: External control over binding start (DRA, etc.)\n6. **Error recovery**: Unreserve cleanup on any phase failure\n\nThis design achieves high scheduling throughput while maintaining correctness and allowing extensibility via plugins.\n",

Waits on permit.WaitingPods map for pod's UID\n    - Returns Success (approved) or Rejected (denied)\n\n17. **Scheduler.bind()** (schedule_one.go:958)\n    - **RunBindPlugins()**: Calls Bind plugins\n    - First plugin to return non-Skip binds pod (sets NodeName)\n    - Default Bind plugin writes binding to API server\n\n18. **Framework.RunPostBindPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1304)\n    - Informational only; no failure handling\n    - Plugins can perform cleanup after binding succeeds\n\n### Failure Handling\n19. **Scheduler.handleSchedulingFailure()** (schedule_one.go:1012)\n    - Called when schedulingCycle fails\n    - If PostFilterPlugins exist, runs preemption to evict lower-priority pods\n    - Calls failure handler which may requeue pod with backoff\n\n20. **Scheduler.handleBindingCycleError()** (schedule_one.go:324)\n    - Called when bindingCycle fails\n    - Cleans up: RunReservePluginsUnreserve() + ForgetPod()\n    - Moves related pods from unschedulable queue back to active/backoff queue\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Pattern: Two-Phase Scheduling with Optimistic Concurrency\n\n**Problem Solved:**\n- Binding is slow (API server write) and can fail\n- Blocking scheduling on binding would be inefficient\n- Need to continue scheduling other pods while binding completes\n\n**Solution:**\n1. **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Find node and assume pod on it in cache\n2. **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Actually bind pod to cluster, with failure recovery\n\n**Key Insight:** Cache assumption creates optimistic lock\n- Pod is considered scheduled in cache immediately\n- Other pods can't use same resources (Assume adds pod to nodeInfo)\n- If binding fails, Forget removes pod and resources are returned to unschedulable queue\n- Other pods scheduled during binding period already see reserved resources\n\n### Plugin Framework: Extension Points\n\nThe framework defines **13 extension points** where plugins can hook in:\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous):**\n- **PreFilter**: Early filtering (can skip Filter plugins entirely)\n- **Filter**: Feasibility check per node\n- **PostFilter**: Preemption/remediation if pod unschedulable\n- **PreScore**: Preparation before scoring (informational)\n- **Score**: Rank nodes 0-100 (parallel per plugin, serial per node)\n- **Reserve**: Resource booking after node chosen\n\n**Permit/Waiting:**\n- **Permit**: Gate before binding (can wait for external events)\n\n**Binding Cycle (Async):**\n- **PreBind**: Pre-binding setup (can still reject)\n- **Bind**: Actually bind pod (default writes to API server)\n- **PostBind**: Cleanup after successful binding (no failures)\n\n**Queue Management:**\n- **PreEnqueue**: Pre-enqueue filtering\n- **QueueSort**: Pod priority ordering\n- **EnqueueExtensions**: Event-driven requeuing hints\n\n### Component Interactions\n\n**1. SchedulingQueue \u2194 Scheduler**\n- Queue holds unscheduled pods in activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulableQ\n- Scheduler.NextPod() pops highest-priority pod\n- Queue.Done(uid) marks pod done after binding\n- Queue.Activate() moves pods between queues on cluster events\n\n**2. Cache \u2194 Framework**\n- Cache maintains assumed pod state and node information\n- UpdateSnapshot() captures cache state at scheduling cycle start\n- Framework.SnapshotSharedLister() provides read-only view to plugins\n- AssumePod() is called after Reserve plugins pass\n- ForgetPod() reverts assumption on failure\n\n**3. CycleState \u2194 Plugins**\n- CycleState is thread-safe mutable map passed to each plugin\n- PreFilter plugins write initial computed state\n- Filter/Score plugins read and optionally update state\n- Reserve/Permit plugins register cleanup actions\n- PreFilterExtensions use state for incremental updates during preemption\n\n**4. Framework \u2194 Extenders**\n- Legacy extensibility mechanism (pre-plugin era)\n- Extenders participate in Filter and Prioritize phases\n- Extenders run after framework plugins\n- Integration: DefaultPreemption plugin can coordinate with extenders\n\n### Data Flow: Pod Perspective\n\n```\nPod \u2192 SchedulingQueue (activeQ)\n   \u2193\nPod.Pop() \u2192 ScheduleOne()\n   \u2193\nScheduling Cycle:\n   - PreFilter plugins: Extract pod requirements, filter nodes\n   - Filter plugins: Test pod feasibility on remaining nodes (parallel)\n   - PreScore plugins: Setup scoring state (informational)\n   - Score plugins: Rank feasible nodes (parallel per plugin)\n   \u2193\n   Find best node via selectHost() \u2192 Assume pod on node in cache\n   \u2193\n   Reserve plugins: Book resources\n   Permit plugins: Gate binding\n   \u2193 (if all pass)\n   Binding Cycle (async goroutine):\n   - WaitOnPermit(): Wait for permit plugin approval\n   - PreBind plugins: Final checks\n   - Bind plugins: Write binding to API server\n   - PostBind plugins: Cleanup\n   \u2193\nPod is scheduled (NodeName set, binding recorded)\n```\n\n### Parallelization Strategy\n\n**Parallel Operations:**\n- **Filter plugins**: Parallelized across nodes (via parallelize.Parallelizer)\n  - Each node tests all filter plugins sequentially\n  - Early termination stops other nodes if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached\n- **Score plugins**: Parallelized across nodes\n  - Each score plugin evaluates all nodes in parallel\n  - NormalizeScore is sequential per plugin\n- **Extenders**: Parallelized across extenders (via goroutines)\n  - Each extender runs independently with mutex for aggregating scores\n\n**Sequential Operations:**\n- Filter plugins per node (can't parallelize within single node)\n- PreFilter and PostFilter plugins (must run sequentially, early termination possible)\n- Reserve, Permit, PreBind plugins (state dependencies)\n\n### Error Handling Strategy\n\n**Success Paths:**\n- All PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit plugins return Success \u2192 pod assigned\n\n**Failure Paths:**\n\n1. **PreFilter or Filter Failure:**\n   - Triggers PostFilter plugins (preemption)\n   - PostFilter plugins can attempt to make pod schedulable\n   - If PostFilter returns Success + NominatingInfo, pod saved for retry\n   - If PostFilter returns Unschedulable, pod goes to unschedulableQ + backoff\n\n2. **Reserve Failure:**\n   - Immediately triggers Unreserve on all prior Reserve plugins\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod requeued to backoffQ\n\n3. **Permit Failure:**\n   - Same cleanup as Reserve failure\n   - If rejected, pod marked and won't be re-tried immediately\n\n4. **Binding Cycle Failure:**\n   - Reserve plugins Unreserved\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod moved to unschedulableQ or backoffQ based on failure reason\n   - Cluster events may trigger requeuing\n\n### Status Codes and Their Meanings\n\n- **Success**: Plugin succeeded, pod can continue or is OK\n- **Error**: Unexpected internal error; pod requeued to activeQ/backoffQ\n- **Unschedulable**: Pod can't fit but may fit after cluster changes (e.g., node capacity increases); pod backed off\n- **UnschedulableAndUnresolvable**: Pod fundamentally unschedulable; pod backed off but PostFilter won't help\n- **Wait** (Permit only): Pod waiting for external event; entered waiting pod map\n- **Skip**: PreFilter/PreScore can skip coupled Filter/Score plugins; BindPlugin can skip binding\n- **Pending** (Reserve/PreBind only): Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external component (e.g., DRA device driver)\n\n### Snapshot Design: Read-Consistency Guarantee\n\n**Why Snapshots?**\n- Plugins run over many milliseconds; cluster state changes during scheduling\n- Without snapshot, plugins could see inconsistent state\n- Snapshot provides frozen view at cycle start\n\n**When Taken:**\n- At start of schedulePod(): `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(nodeInfoSnapshot)`\n- Snapshot remains unchanged through PreFilter \u2192 Filter \u2192 PreScore \u2192 Score\n\n**Snapshot Guarantees:**\n- All Filter decisions based on same node state\n- Score plugins see same node state\n- If pod preempted nodes before score phase, preemption not reflected in snapshot\n\n**Binding Phase:**\n- Can't use snapshot (cluster state has changed during scoring)\n- Plugins use live informers instead\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase architecture combining **synchronous scheduling (find + assume) with asynchronous binding**. This decouples slow API operations from scheduling throughput.\n\nThe **plugin framework** provides 13 extension points with clear separation of concerns: filtering (feasibility), scoring (preference), reservation (resource booking), and binding (commitment). Plugins are orchestrated via a state machine with careful failure handling and recovery mechanisms.\n\n**Key architectural decisions:**\n1. **Optimistic concurrency**: Assume in cache, recover on binding failure\n2. **Snapshot consistency**: Frozen cache view for scheduling decisions\n3. **Progressive filtering**: Early termination when enough feasible nodes found\n4. **Parallel scoring**: Independent plugin evaluation across nodes\n5. **Permit gating**: External control over binding start (DRA, etc.)\n6. **Error recovery**: Unreserve cleanup on any phase failure\n\nThis design achieves high scheduling throughput while maintaining correctness and allowing extensibility via plugins.\n",

# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis

## Files Examined

### Core Scheduler Files
- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main Scheduler struct that orchestrates the scheduling loop, initializes frameworks, queues, and cache; implements the Run() method that starts the scheduling process
- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Contains ScheduleOne() entry point and the two-phase scheduling pipeline (schedulingCycle and bindingCycle); implements findNodesThatFitPod, prioritizeNodes, selectHost

### Framework Architecture
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), Framework interface, CycleState, Status codes, and extension points
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — frameworkImpl implementation that instantiates and orchestrates plugins; implements all Run* methods (RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins, etc.)
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — CycleState passes mutable data between plugins within a scheduling cycle

### Internal Components
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** — Cache interface defining pod/node state management with Assume/Forget/Add/Remove operations and snapshot semantics
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — Cache implementation tracking assumed pods and node information with expiration policy
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Snapshot provides read-only view of cache state at beginning of scheduling cycle
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue manages pods to be scheduled with activeQ, backoffQ, and unschedulableQ; handles pod lifecycle
